  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_1168a086-053c-4af0-93a7-4b55f54de19a'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText4973773185233904666" style="display:none">Don Tillman and Rosie Jarman are back. The Wife Project is complete, and Don and Rosie are happily married and living in New York. But they're about to face a new challenge because - surprise - Rosie is pregnant. <br /><br />Don sets about learning the protocols of becoming a father, but his unusual research style gets him into trouble with the law. Fortunately his best friend Gene is on hand to offer advice: he's left Claudia and moved in with Don and Rosie. <br /><br />As Don tries to schedule time for pregnancy research, getting Gene and Claudia to reconcile, servicing the industrial refrigeration unit that occupies half his apartment, helping Dave the Baseball Fan save his business, and staying on the right side of Lydia the social worker, he almost misses the biggest problem of all: he might lose Rosie when she needs him the most.</span>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('edition_22382317').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_22382317').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('edition_22382317').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

</script></div>

    <a title="Sam Quixote" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5759543-sam-quixote"><img alt="Sam Quixote" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529183438p2/5759543.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1065543440?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sam Quixote" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sam Quixote" href="/user/show/5759543-sam-quixote">Sam Quixote</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/22382317-the-rosie-effect">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1065543440&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1065543440" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4170041185719352404">After the success of The Rosie Project last year, it was inevitable that we’d get a sequel, though so soon was surprising. In The Rosie Project we followed the adventures of Don Tillman, a genetics professor (with probable Aspergers) who went looking for a wife and found one in Rosie, who drew him into her own quest to find her unknown biological father. <br/><br/>In The Rosie Effect, Rosie is pregnant and Don is going to be a father. I’m going to stop there because this relates to my biggest problem with</span>
  <span id="freeText4170041185719352404" style="display:none">After the success of The Rosie Project last year, it was inevitable that we’d get a sequel, though so soon was surprising. In The Rosie Project we followed the adventures of Don Tillman, a genetics professor (with probable Aspergers) who went looking for a wife and found one in Rosie, who drew him into her own quest to find her unknown biological father. <br /><br />In The Rosie Effect, Rosie is pregnant and Don is going to be a father. I’m going to stop there because this relates to my biggest problem with the book. There are numerous problems with this novel - in fact, I can’t name a single positive about it - and everything about it totally stinks but my biggest issue with this novel is the total lack of a plot. <br /><br />See how I summarised The Rosie Project - it sounds like a real novel right, with a story? Then see how I tried to summarise The Rosie Effect - one line about Rosie being pregnant - and stopped. Because there is no plot to this book and that’s why it’s such a tedious read. <br /><br />Don and Rosie are in New York, Rosie’s pursuing her degree, Don’s doing his genetics stuff, Gene, Don’s philandering colleague, joins them because his wife kicked him out. This isn’t plot, it’s just setup. Don’s friends with a guy who installs refrigeration systems and happens to have done a big job for an old rock drummer called George. And this brings me to the next problem with the book - zero conflict. <br /><br />There is never a single problem in the “story” that Don doesn’t deal with easily, or Simsion magically solves for Don. Don and Rosie need a place to stay? Well, Don happens to know a guy who knows a rock drummer who is obsessed with beer and has an entire apartment below his attached to his beer cellar - they could stay in the spacious new apartment for free and Don could monitor the temperature of the beer for him! Well isn’t that convenient! <br /><br />Simsion contrives numerous “obstacles” for Don to overcome that essentially end with “and the person realised it was a stupid novelistic contrivance designed to eat up pages before waving Don on”. For instance, a social worker - based on nothing more than Don’s unknowing ordering of an unecological dish - sets out to cause problems for him, threatening to deport him being as he is an Aussie living in America. <br /><br />This allows Simsion to insert a well-used sitcom trope of having someone impersonating someone else, in this case one of Don’s friends pretending to be Rosie because Don doesn’t want to cause Rosie any extra stress that might harm the baby. How does that storyline end? Eh, turns out it doesn’t really matter. Social worker admits to behaving irrationally, falls for Gene, the end. <br /><br />Arguably the worst offender out of these contrivances is the fact that, in the third act, Simsion realised he didn’t have any dramatic way of building to the finale because he hadn’t bothered with any story up to that point. So he invents some nonsense about Rosie suddenly thinking that Don won’t make a good husband, so she decides to leave him and go back to Australia. It’s so awkward and out of the blue, it’s staggering - really? We’re supposed to believe this crap out of nowhere?!<br /><br />This leads to another “really?” moment when Don runs to the airport to profess his love for Rosie. I couldn’t believe the cheesiest of all cheeseball scenes was this book’s finale, but it was. The guy running to the airport at the last minute to tell the girl he loved her. Absolutely horrendous. And then what happens? Rosie realises that oh yeah, suddenly leaving Don didn’t really make sense and she still loved him and it was all for nothing. <br /><br />Then there are the character problems of this book. Don, for example, is never explicitly said to have Aspergers or Autism, even if he sounds like Data from Star Trek all of the time (“Greetings!”). He can’t identify facial features, he doesn’t understand human emotions, most of the time doesn’t even seem to possess them, he looks at people and instantly calculates their BMIs, he doesn’t even understand certain social situations as being inappropriate, such as a man with a camera on his own sitting on a park bench taking pictures of children in the playground - but he’s definitely not autistic!! <br /><br />This is another example of Simsion’s shoddy writing. Don is autistic and/or has Aspergers - he’s somewhere on the autistic spectrum anyway - but he also reacts like a human when he needs to. In other words, Simsion wants to have his cake and eat it. <br /><br />But at least Don seems like a character and perhaps Gene too. The rest of the cast? There’s a trio of scientists Don labels B1, B2, and B3 because they all have names beginning with B, but also because he can’t identify faces (he’s definitely not autistic or anything!!) - and that’s how I feel all of the characters should’ve been labelled, rather than given names, because they don’t seem like characters at all. Most damningly, Rosie herself is a two-dimensional placeholder character - she’s the stock pregnant woman. She doesn’t seem like a real person, or distinctively her own person, she’s merely The Pregnant Woman in the book. That is, when she’s not behaving like a total bitch in total contrast to her character in the first book but maybe that’s the hormones or something?<br /><br />Those are the main problems with The Rosie Effect though really there are too many faults all the way through this to list. And it’s labelled a romantic comedy? I suppose the romance is there, generic though it may be (airport scene!), but comedy? I never laughed once, nor did it seem that there was anything to laugh at. Was the fact that Don was photographing kids in the park, unaware that this made him look like a pedo, meant to be hilarious? Because to me it just underlined the fact that this guy needed a carer more than anything (but he’s definitely not autistic!!). <br /><br />And it’s boring - my god, this book is boring! All of the problems - the lack of story, the dull characters, the absence of humour, the contrivances and cliches - compound massively on the book, one after the other, until it’s near unbearable to read! It’s so poorly written with zero imagination or skill that it reads like a first draft than the final finished product. <br /><br />In the end, it’s very clear that The Rosie Effect was rushed out because everyone involved wanted to capitalise on the financial success of The Rosie Project. Except the sequel is a charmless, humourless chore to struggle through - an unending, uninteresting slog through totally artless, unengaging garbage. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4170041185719352404" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_982036178" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/982036178" />
    <a title="Natalie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7812107-natalie"><img alt="Natalie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1480197403p2/7812107.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/982036178?book_show_action=true">Jun 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie" href="/user/show/7812107-natalie">Natalie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781476767314" href="/book/show/22546489-the-rosie-effect">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7812107-natalie?shelf=the-anticipation-is-killing-me">the-anticipation-is-killing-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7812107-natalie?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7812107-natalie?shelf=character-love">character-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7812107-natalie?shelf=author-love">author-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7812107-natalie?shelf=a-boy-s-pov">a-boy-s-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7812107-natalie?shelf=aussie">aussie</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer982036178" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11555067329566544420">I loved <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16181775.The_Rosie_Project__Don_Tillman__1_' title='The Rosie Project (Don Tillman #1) by Graeme Simsion' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Rosie Project</a>. Don Tillman was a character unlike any I had ever encountered before. Honest, hilarious, and easy to love (for the reader, not necessarily for the characters in the book). I was beyond excited when I heard there would be a second book. I was also a little apprehensive, which happens when I finish a book that I thought would be a stand-alone and that was <i>amazing</i> as a stand-alone.<br/><br/>After reading reviews that gave only a couple stars or only <i>one</i> star, I was downright SCARED</span>
  <span id="freeText11555067329566544420" style="display:none">I loved <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16181775.The_Rosie_Project__Don_Tillman__1_" title="The Rosie Project (Don Tillman #1) by Graeme Simsion" rel="nofollow noopener">The Rosie Project</a>. Don Tillman was a character unlike any I had ever encountered before. Honest, hilarious, and easy to love (for the reader, not necessarily for the characters in the book). I was beyond excited when I heard there would be a second book. I was also a little apprehensive, which happens when I finish a book that I thought would be a stand-alone and that was <i>amazing</i> as a stand-alone.<br><br>After reading reviews that gave only a couple stars or only <i>one</i> star, I was downright SCARED and took my time getting around to reading it. <br><br>All I can say is: <b>WHY THE HECK DID I WAIT SO LONG?</b><br><br>Wait. I can also say: <br><br><b>TO THE TWO STAR REVIEWS:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1448135469ra/17099721.gif" width="350" height="241" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>AND TO THE ONE STAR REVIEWS:</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1448135469ra/17099722.gif" width="345" height="280" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Sorry. I understand that everyone likes different things and has different rating systems, but I am just <i>baffled</i> that people could give something like an unedited erotica novella that uses your instead of you're and this the same number of stars. BAFFLED.<br>OK. Now that I have <i>that</i> out of my system. <br><br>I will be honest and say that because I had read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16181775.The_Rosie_Project__Don_Tillman__1_" title="The Rosie Project (Don Tillman #1) by Graeme Simsion" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Rosie Project</a> so long ago and because my memory gets worse and worse for every year that I age, the details of the first book were a bit fuzzy. However, I was snapped back almost instantly and the voice of Don was as familiar and comforting as a warm, fuzzy blanket. <br><br>I loved Don's thought processes in this book as much as I did in the first. Don is a very <i>clear</i> character. His "voice" is one of the most memorable and easy to fall into of all the characters I've ever encountered. I love the funny situations he gets himself into and want to cheer for him when he is able to get out of them. I love his good intentions. It would be exhausting to be Don, always having to compute what to say/do/think next. <br><br>It is my love for Don's character that made it easy for me to bypass what others seem to have found very frustrating: the lack of or the change in Rosie's character in this book. I believe one reader even described her as being a "bitch" in this one. I didn't find her reactions to be as unbelievable as others. She is pregnant. She is excited about the pregnancy. Many men don't have the same excitement and instant emotional attachment to a pregnancy as women to begin with; Don has an even more difficult time because he has an extremely difficult time <i>feeling/recognizing emotions</i>. It's understandable that she would be upset. It's understandable that she would question what kind of father he would be able to be to their child. <br><br>Is everything that happens believable? No. Does everything align like the stars and the moon? No. But this isn't meant to be a serious scholarly book. This is light - a "beach read" if you will (although there are no true beaches here). <br><br>I'm giving this <b>five stars</b> because "I liked it" four stars isn't enough. I find the Don Tillman books to be unique, which is something that is getting harder and harder to find nowadays. <br><br><br><b>--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------</b><br><b>June 30, 2014</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1404140465ra/10196853.gif" width="430" height="242" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Please. Please oh please oh please, Mr. Simsion. Please do not ruin a good thing. <br><br><b>I'm trusting you. <br>No pressure.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="11555067329566544420" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" href="/user/show/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar">Kelly (and the Book Boar)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781922182104" href="/book/show/21844019-the-rosie-effect">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1036185456" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16873948303885409816">Find all of my reviews at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/'>http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br/><br/><a href='http://imgur.com/Zv3ew7h' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1411579130ra/11251272.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Well, rats. Maybe my expectations were just too high after falling head over heels in love with <i>The Rosie Project</i> last year. Maybe there wasn’t enough magic left to make a worthy sequel. Whatever the case, I’m bummed I didn’t enjoy this as much as I thought I would.<br/><br/><b>WARNING: IF YOU HAVE NOT YET READ <i>THE ROSIE PROJECT</i> AND INTEND TO DO SO, BACK AWAY FROM THIS REVIEW IMMEDIATELY. THERE IS ZERO WAY TO AVOID SPOILING THE FIRST BOOK AND S</b></span>
  <span id="freeText16873948303885409816" style="display:none">Find all of my reviews at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/">http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/Zv3ew7h" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1411579130ra/11251272.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Well, rats. Maybe my expectations were just too high after falling head over heels in love with <i>The Rosie Project</i> last year. Maybe there wasn’t enough magic left to make a worthy sequel. Whatever the case, I’m bummed I didn’t enjoy this as much as I thought I would.<br><br><b>WARNING: IF YOU HAVE NOT YET READ <i>THE ROSIE PROJECT</i> AND INTEND TO DO SO, BACK AWAY FROM THIS REVIEW IMMEDIATELY. THERE IS ZERO WAY TO AVOID SPOILING THE FIRST BOOK AND STILL BE ABLE TO WRITE ABOUT THE SECOND.</b><br><br>Still here? Okay, here we go …<br><br>This is the continuation of <s>Sheldon Cooper’s</s> Don Tillman’s story. Now 41, he and Rosie have been married for 10 months (and 10 days, if you want to be technical – which we know Don <b>always</b> wants to be technical). The couple are residing in The Big Apple where Don is an assistant professor at Columbia and Rosie is finishing up her Ph.D. Rosie is about to inform Don that they have a little “something to celebrate.”<br><br>And there’s where our problem begins. While Don remains Don and is completely over-the-top adorkable, getting himself into laugh-out-loudable (new word – add it to the dictionary, Merriam-Webster) pickle after pickle due to his inability to interact successfully with most other humans, Rosie loses her charm and basically becomes a straight-up bitch (I’m sure there are more refined phrases I could use to describe Rosie, but she peeved me off, so I’m not going to). It was impossible for me to read this as just “entertainment” when I was so angry with a main character and none of Don’s antics were enough to keep my spirits up once Rosie entered a scene. That’s not to say Don was without faults . . . Don was <b>FULL</b> of faults. That’s kind of the whole point ; )<br><br><b>WARNING #2: THE FOLLOWING IS <i>REALLY</i> A SPOILER WHICH I HAVE SPOILER-TAGGED IN AN ATTEMPT TO NOT RUIN THIS BOOK FOR EVERYONE. READ AT YOUR OWN RISK.</b><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Rosie commits the ULTIMATE sin of <i>any</i> woman – let alone a married one. She decides (even though she chose someone like Don for a partner and therefore supposedly accepted him as-is, including all of his quirks) that it is “her body, her choice,” stops taking birth control without consulting Don, gets knocked up (even though she’s finishing up a Ph.D. program and then <i>immediately</i> plans on turning around and beginning medical school and has ZERO plans on who will care for the baby/how they will pay for the baby), and then gets mad at Don for not jumping for joy about the situation. It made my heart hurt. It made me think that the author <i>really</i> dislikes women as he puts forth this "surprise baby scenario" as something the average wife does on the regular. It ruined the magic for me and made me soooooo sad. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>I’ve sat on this review for a few days now because my head told me to give it a low rating, but my love for Don told me to keep it high. I’m settling for a 3, but not with a completely clear conscience. If I thought about it any longer it could easily become a 2 (or a 4 – I'm telling you, I have some <i>serious</i> multiple-personality disorder on this one). I won’t be throwing in the towel on Graeme Simsion just yet, but I sure wish he would have given me a little bit more of a “Shamy” vibe like I had been hoping for . . . . <br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/POPZE5c" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1411579130ra/11251273.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/khvq9at" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1411579130ra/11251274.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/bqmBbNs" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1411579130ra/11251275.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>ARC provided by NetGalley in exchange for an honest review. Thank you, NetGalley!!!</i><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/951442725?book_show_action=true">May 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tatiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tatiana" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781476767314" href="/book/show/22546489-the-rosie-effect">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2014">2014</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer951442725" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10893236299038921198">Is the magic gone?<br/><br/>It feels like it is.<br/><br/>Last year, I remember thinking that “The Rosie Project” was my favorite chick lit book ever, which was ironic because it had been written by a man. I thought it was hilarious and original.<br/><br/>This year, after reading “The Rosie Effect,” I am asking myself – was the first book much better or I just read it at the time when I had a better mood for it?<br/><br/>I don’t know. But reading “The Rosie Effect” just wasn’t the same. I didn’t find it funny, the jokes felt old and r</span>
  <span id="freeText10893236299038921198" style="display:none">Is the magic gone?<br /><br />It feels like it is.<br /><br />Last year, I remember thinking that “The Rosie Project” was my favorite chick lit book ever, which was ironic because it had been written by a man. I thought it was hilarious and original.<br /><br />This year, after reading “The Rosie Effect,” I am asking myself – was the first book much better or I just read it at the time when I had a better mood for it?<br /><br />I don’t know. But reading “The Rosie Effect” just wasn’t the same. I didn’t find it funny, the jokes felt old and repetitive, the whole plot sluggish and strained. It mostly felt like a recycled-trope kind of sequel and it didn’t charm me anymore.<br /><br />Frankly, I doubt that if Graeme Simsion comes up with another sequel I will care to check it out. </span>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_943726684" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/943726684" />
    <a title="ALPHAreader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4285990-alphareader"><img alt="ALPHAreader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457410626p2/4285990.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/943726684?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ALPHAreader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ALPHAreader" href="/user/show/4285990-alphareader">ALPHAreader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781922182104" href="/book/show/21844019-the-rosie-effect">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer943726684" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4849369819287570491">'The Rosie Effect' is the sequel to Graeme Simsion’s 2013 internationally best-selling novel 'The Rosie Project', which I <a href='http://alphareader.blogspot.com.au/2013/03/the-rosie-project-by-graeme-simsion.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>enjoyed </a>immensely (as did <a href='http://www.gatesnotes.com/Books/The-Rosie-Project' rel='nofollow noopener'>Bill Gates</a>). <br/>I had been very excited to read its sequel and revisit Don and Rosie – and I said as much in my 'Rosie Project' review. <br/><br/>But now I have read the sequel, and I did not care for it. <br/><br/>Allow me to try and relay the things I did not enjoy about this book, and assign them some sort of quantifiable value. I shall list what I did not like, and use</span>
  <span id="freeText4849369819287570491" style="display:none">'The Rosie Effect' is the sequel to Graeme Simsion’s 2013 internationally best-selling novel 'The Rosie Project', which I <a href="http://alphareader.blogspot.com.au/2013/03/the-rosie-project-by-graeme-simsion.html" rel="nofollow noopener">enjoyed </a>immensely (as did <a href="http://www.gatesnotes.com/Books/The-Rosie-Project" rel="nofollow noopener">Bill Gates</a>). <br />I had been very excited to read its sequel and revisit Don and Rosie – and I said as much in my 'Rosie Project' review. <br /><br />But now I have read the sequel, and I did not care for it. <br /><br />Allow me to try and relay the things I did not enjoy about this book, and assign them some sort of quantifiable value. I shall list what I did not like, and use a percentage marker to indicate how much their inclusion annoyed me and affected my enjoyment of 'The Rosie Effect'. <br /><br /><b>•	The Baby Project – 5% </b><br />'The Rosie Project' was about geneticist Don Tillman concocting a scientific survey to find the perfect wife. He found an imperfectly-perfect wife in Rosie Jarman, who failed at his Wife Project but succeeded in the hands-on role. 'The Rosie Effect' begins when Don and Rosie are happily married and living in New York – Don is a professor at Columbia and Rosie is completing her PhD. It is not a good time for them to “get pregnant”, but that’s exactly what happens … which triggers The Baby Project – which sees Don attempt to prepare for impending fatherhood by conducting extensive research into everything from suitable diet for Rosie to child-rearing techniques. Don is particularly keen to conduct such research because of an altercation with a friend-of-a-friend, who states that Don would make an unsuitable parent. <br />It follows that after The Wife Project comes The Baby Project (as indicated by famous rhyme: first comes loves, then comes marriage etc, etc, etc…) but this storyline quickly falters, and the book started to feel like the nine-month gestation period itself. Or, as Alfred Hickling for <a href="http://www.theguardian.com/books/2014/oct/08/the-rosie-effect-graeme-simsion-review" rel="nofollow noopener">The Guardian</a> noted: “it fulfils a formula familiar to many sequels of bestelling novels in that it is twice as long and only half as good.” <br /><br /><b>•	Gregory Peck – 25%</b><br />Simsion repeats many jokes in this book. The Gregory Peck ha-ha was particularly annoying for it’s repetitiveness.<br />Rosie thinks that Don bears a resemblance to the famous actor Gregory Peck (circa: 'To Kill a Mockingbird'). This was a lovely visual in 'The Rosie Project'. In 'The Rosie Effect' we learn that Don has taken his resemblance and amplified it by repeating famous lines from Gregory Peck films ('Roman Holiday' in particular) which often results in Rosie feeling amorous towards Don. This is nice, and when Don first mentions his subtle ‘strategy’ it’s funny, and I cracked a smile … but Simsion repeats a variation of this joke about 20 times throughout the book.<br />It is a sad day when mention of Gregory Peck in a novel becomes frustrating. <br />A sad day indeed. <br /><br /><b>•	Marital Violence joke – 35%</b><br />It’s not just the Gregory Peck joke that Simsion repeats.<br />There are two elaborate comedy-of-errors situations that take quite a bit of build-up, but the premise is people thinking that Don means to do some sort of harm to Rosie and/or the baby. He doesn’t. The misunderstanding comes from Don being somewhere on the autism spectrum (what was once called Asperger syndrome) and being entirely too honest and direct with people, particularly those in positions of authority. This sees him participating in a domestic violence counselling session, and giving the wrong impression to a flight marshal about intending to hurt Rosie. <br />This “funny” clunked on the page … twice.<br /><br /><b>•	'The Rosie Project' similarities – 10%</b><br />A lot of The Rosie Effect is set-up to be a mirrored sequel to 'The Rosie Project'. The Wife/Baby Project plot is just one of them. Simsion reuses another in the friendly neighbour who Don becomes emotionally (unbeknownst to him) attached to. In 'Rosie Project' Don’s kind, elderly neighbour Daphne was the person who encouraged him to become a husband … hence, The Wife Project. Simsion conveniently contrives a similar scenario for Don in 'The Rosie Effect', except this time the neighbour is an old rocker called George who has his own family dilemmas and both gives Don advice, and benefits from Don’s “boy’s night out” initiative. George also provides Don and Rosie an unrealistic housing opportunity in New York. <br />I didn’t love the skewed-slightly plot, especially since George didn’t hold a candle to Daphne who was a crucial part of Don’s character arc. <br /><br /><b>•	Gene – 5%</b><br />Gene’s wife, Claudia, finally leaves the serial-philanderer and Don convinces Gene to come and take a position at Columbia and stay with him and Rosie. <br />This book is in no way improved by more Gene. <br />… I don’t think anything is ever improved by more Gene. <br /><br /><b>•	The Women – 20%</b><br />This is a very male-centric story. Don spends a lot of “boys nights out” with his friends George, Gene and new acquaintance Dave working through various husband and fatherhood difficulties. By comparison, Rosie actually feels like a depleted character in this book – it didn’t feel like she was physically present for a lot of it (and probably wasn’t, as she’s frequently working on her thesis) – but emotionally it felt like Simsion left her to lag behind. Maybe this is because he writes her as a silly pregnant woman – irrational, baby-brained and forever frustrated – rather than an actual human being who we’ve come to know and love through Don’s search for her in 'The Rosie Project'. As Helen Elliott said in her <a href="http://www.smh.com.au/entertainment/books/graeme-simsion-looks-for-the-rosie-effect-again-20140919-10j82b.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Sydney Morning Herald</a> review: "If ever there was a formulaic pregnancy, this is it. It might make men laugh. Women will be unamused and even cross."<br />Other women in the book are equally hollow – there’s the second emotionally overwrought pregnant woman (Sonia), evil professional lady (Lydia), Skype-chat ex (Claudia) or simply background extras B1, B2 and B3 (I’m not kidding). <br /><br /><b>100% disappointed. </b><br /><br />I didn’t like 'The Rosie Effect'. I first became worried when I got to Chapter Eight and realised I hadn’t chuckled once – compared to my belly-laughing by that point in 'The Rosie Project'. <br />Sure, a few scenes elicited smiles:<br /><br /><i>Loud Woman laughed. Loudly. ‘He’s Rain Man! You know. Dustin Hoffman when he remembers all the cards. Dan’s the cocktail Rain Man.’<br />Rain Man! I had seen the film. I did not identify in any way with Rain Man, who was inarticulate, dependent and unemployable. A society of Rain Men would be dysfunctional. A society of Don Tillmans would be efficient, safe and pleasant for all of us. </i><br /><br />But they were far and few between.<br /><br />To be honest, I rushed through reading the end because I just wanted to be done with it. I still think Don is a great character, and I will pick up the third book when it comes out … but I might have to rein in my expectations, and I suggest you do the same if you’re going into 'The Rosie Effect'. <br /><br />1.5-2/5 <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4849369819287570491" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1069896774?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Phrynne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Phrynne" href="/user/show/8655084-phrynne">Phrynne</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1069896774" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6262093728212417717">I raced through this book and enjoyed every word. There were many laugh aloud moments and lots of those delightful sequences where Don manages to land on his feet despite everything.<br/><br/> This book becomes much more serious than <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16181775.The_Rosie_Project__Don_Tillman___1_' title='The Rosie Project (Don Tillman, #1) by Graeme Simsion' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Rosie Project</a> though and there are some sad and some stressful moments too. I was not happy with the character of Rosie for much of the book. She seemed to have lost her high spirits and her understanding of Don somewhere along the way and at times I wanted to give her a </span>
  <span id="freeText6262093728212417717" style="display:none">I raced through this book and enjoyed every word. There were many laugh aloud moments and lots of those delightful sequences where Don manages to land on his feet despite everything.<br /><br /> This book becomes much more serious than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16181775.The_Rosie_Project__Don_Tillman___1_" title="The Rosie Project (Don Tillman, #1) by Graeme Simsion" rel="nofollow noopener">The Rosie Project</a> though and there are some sad and some stressful moments too. I was not happy with the character of Rosie for much of the book. She seemed to have lost her high spirits and her understanding of Don somewhere along the way and at times I wanted to give her a good shake. Don on the other hand was always just himself and Gene almost redeemed his character along the way.<br /><br /> A really enjoyable read.</span>

<div id="review_935779556" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/935779556" />
    <a title="Rebecca" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5875398-rebecca"><img alt="Rebecca" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599578317p2/5875398.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/935779556?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca" href="/user/show/5875398-rebecca">Rebecca</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781443435925" href="/book/show/21936708-the-rosie-effect">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5875398-rebecca?shelf=laugh-out-loud">laugh-out-loud</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5875398-rebecca?shelf=read-via-edelweiss">read-via-edelweiss</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5875398-rebecca?shelf=autism">autism</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer935779556" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9158891286346088125"><b>(3.5)</b> I was wary after the <a href='http://www.theguardian.com/books/2014/oct/08/the-rosie-effect-graeme-simsion-review' rel='nofollow noopener'><i>Guardian</i> review</a> called this sequel “twice as long and only half as good” as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/547817378' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Rosie Project</a>, but I actually enjoyed it just about as much as the original. In a new NYC setting, Rosie’s unplanned pregnancy has Don Tillman – and everyone else around him – assessing his suitability for fatherhood. He manages to supplement his textbook knowledge of obstetrics with some bizarre practical experience, such as assisting with a lesbian parenting study and having a hand in a (</span>
  <span id="freeText9158891286346088125" style="display:none"><b>(3.5)</b> I was wary after the <a href="http://www.theguardian.com/books/2014/oct/08/the-rosie-effect-graeme-simsion-review" rel="nofollow noopener"><i>Guardian</i> review</a> called this sequel “twice as long and only half as good” as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/547817378" rel="nofollow noopener">The Rosie Project</a>, but I actually enjoyed it just about as much as the original. In a new NYC setting, Rosie’s unplanned pregnancy has Don Tillman – and everyone else around him – assessing his suitability for fatherhood. He manages to supplement his textbook knowledge of obstetrics with some bizarre practical experience, such as assisting with a lesbian parenting study and having a hand in a (bovine) delivery. Expect much madcap hilarity.<br /><br />“My innate logical skills were significantly greater than my interpersonal skills,” Don notes in typical deadpan style, but by helping friends old and new he has some success in developing empathy. Whether this is believable for a character with Asperger’s I couldn’t say with any authority, but it makes for an emotionally satisfying storyline.<br /><br />My favorite lines: “A society of Rain Men would be dysfunctional. A society of Don Tillmans would be efficient, safe, and pleasant for all of us.” As a big fan of appropriate fetus names, I also appreciated Don and Rosie’s choice of “Bud” (= Baby Under Development, but also fits cleverly with ‘Rosie’ and indicates friendly informality).<br /><br />Where could the series go next?</span>
  <a data-text-id="9158891286346088125" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_950354304" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/950354304" />
    <a title="Suzanne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11889829-suzanne"><img alt="Suzanne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593566451p2/11889829.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/950354304?book_show_action=true">May 28, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Suzanne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Suzanne" href="/user/show/11889829-suzanne">Suzanne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781922182104" href="/book/show/21844019-the-rosie-effect">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11889829-suzanne?shelf=signed-copy">signed-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11889829-suzanne?shelf=owned">owned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer950354304" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14715198307108530682">Don Tillman what a guy. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1895943.Graeme_Simsion' title='Graeme Simsion' rel='nofollow noopener'>Graeme Simsion</a> what a guy. I attended the Sydney launch of this book, so was really happy and interested to hear the background story of the author, and how <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19093648.The_Rosie_Project' title='The Rosie Project by Graeme Simsion' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Rosie Project</a> was bought to life, as well as this lovely second half. Don Tillman is such a quirky character, that I can see it took someone as equally charming and full of life as the author to bring this character into our lives, so many lives as it has - it's a very popular set of books and fans around the worl</span>
  <span id="freeText14715198307108530682" style="display:none">Don Tillman what a guy. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1895943.Graeme_Simsion" title="Graeme Simsion" rel="nofollow noopener">Graeme Simsion</a> what a guy. I attended the Sydney launch of this book, so was really happy and interested to hear the background story of the author, and how <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19093648.The_Rosie_Project" title="The Rosie Project by Graeme Simsion" rel="nofollow noopener">The Rosie Project</a> was bought to life, as well as this lovely second half. Don Tillman is such a quirky character, that I can see it took someone as equally charming and full of life as the author to bring this character into our lives, so many lives as it has - it's a very popular set of books and fans around the world will understand why. I recommend re reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19093648.The_Rosie_Project" title="The Rosie Project by Graeme Simsion" rel="nofollow noopener">The Rosie Project</a>, as the book is full of fun characters that to re visit them will really do its sequel justice. This time around I didn't enjoy the character of Rosie as much, she was somewhat unrelenting in her lack of compassion for the man she knew was very 'different' when she agreed to marry him, and as for the pregnancy, this was an odd situation to spring on our beloved Don. Although the entire book revolves around the issue! This book was a very enjoyable read, I don't think anything can top <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19093648.The_Rosie_Project" title="The Rosie Project by Graeme Simsion" rel="nofollow noopener">The Rosie Project</a>, but I did not expect it to in any way, but it was the perfect sequel to a very special book. A fantastic theme these books address perfectly is the realm of issues that people all around the world face with mental illness, and that is a very important and worthy outcome. All Aussies will love this, as I'm sure people all around the world will, so if you haven't had the pleasure of meeting this series yet, I would highly recommend it to everyone. Loved the characters and loved the whole fun ride!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14715198307108530682" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1266410398" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1266410398" />
    <a title="Darth J " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18974711-darth-j"><img alt="Darth J " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1456429148p2/18974711.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1266410398?book_show_action=true">Apr 28, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Darth J " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Darth J " href="/user/show/18974711-darth-j">Darth J </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781476767314" href="/book/show/22546489-the-rosie-effect">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1266410398" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12543424571494915295">Have you ever watched <i>Curb Your Enthusiasm</i>? I liken this book to that only in the way that you can see the train wreck happening from a mile away but it’s going to happen anyway and you can’t look away even though the anxiety of the awkward social situation is just burning a hole in your stomach. Unfortunately, <i>The Rosie Effect</i> is <b>not</b> like <i>Curb</i> in that it’s just not funny or entertaining. I should have listened to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1036185456?book_show_action=false&page=1' rel='nofollow noopener'>Kelly</a> before I read this.<br/><br/>Anyway, what I choose to write my review on is the confli</span>
  <span id="freeText12543424571494915295" style="display:none">Have you ever watched <i>Curb Your Enthusiasm</i>? I liken this book to that only in the way that you can see the train wreck happening from a mile away but it’s going to happen anyway and you can’t look away even though the anxiety of the awkward social situation is just burning a hole in your stomach. Unfortunately, <i>The Rosie Effect</i> is <b>not</b> like <i>Curb</i> in that it’s just not funny or entertaining. I should have listened to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1036185456?book_show_action=false&amp;page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Kelly</a> before I read this.<br><br>Anyway, what I choose to write my review on is the conflict in this story that falls on the feet of a despicable character named Lydia. Ugh, this woman is just obnoxious! She’s one of the worst kinds of people imaginable; She condescends to others and uses guilt tactics without being completely informed (but of course she thinks she knows it all and will not listen to logic…), is pretentious, and she abuses her power. She’s basically that smug Gwyneth Paltrow, so full of herself and out of touch with reality and still sets herself on a pedestal. Ugh.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1430494451i/14718426._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I do love it when she gets some shade thrown at her though by Seymour at a lunch when she goes on a rant against people with Asperger’s:<br><blockquote>”You want some guy with Asperger’s flying your plane?” said Lydia<br>“Better than someone who uses words they don’t understand,” said Seymour. (p. 64)</blockquote><br><br>That’s the only interesting part of this story. The rest was bland and a bore to read. Even Rosie—who is now pregnant—is basically used as a prop for most of the book, Gene’s wife finally kicks him out for being a skeeze, and Don is breaking people down (<i>Charlie’s Angels</i> style) when he’s not Sheldoning around.<br><br><u>My advice:</u> stick with the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1257292988?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">first book</a> and treat it as a stand-alone because the sequel is a waste of time to read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12543424571494915295" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1038939145" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781476767314" href="/book/show/22546489-the-rosie-effect">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/188447-jessica-jeffers?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/188447-jessica-jeffers?shelf=edelweiss">edelweiss</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1038939145" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3772742230875233092">I am such an asshole. <br/><br/>I think I was among the minority of readers who wasn’t blown away by <i>The Rosie Project</i>. I thought that it was rather sweet at times, but the character development didn't always feel natural. Even taking into consideration the idea that you have to compromise and address personal issues before you can be successful with relationships, the changes the characters underwent for the sake of the plot just struck me as stretching credulity a little too much. <br/><br/>So if <i>The Rosie Projec</i></span>
  <span id="freeText3772742230875233092" style="display:none">I am such an asshole. <br /><br />I think I was among the minority of readers who wasn’t blown away by <i>The Rosie Project</i>. I thought that it was rather sweet at times, but the character development didn't always feel natural. Even taking into consideration the idea that you have to compromise and address personal issues before you can be successful with relationships, the changes the characters underwent for the sake of the plot just struck me as stretching credulity a little too much. <br /><br />So if <i>The Rosie Project</i> was seen as essentially Sheldon Cooper Falls in Love, then this is essentially Sheldon Cooper Has A Baby. <br /><br />Here, Rosie announces she's pregnant ten months into their marriage. She and Don are living in New York, where he's working in a lab and she's finishing her PhD/MD at Columbia. Both halves of the couple have doubts and insecurities about their impending parenthood, and Don tries to address these insecurities in the same methodological, overly rational way he addresses everything. Hijinks and calamities ensue, leading to extra tension in already tense marriage. <br /><br />I didn’t enjoy this book really at all, primarily because Don’s “quirkiness” has gone over the top to the point where it’s more annoying than charming. I also don’t think that the people in his life would realistically just go along with him to the extent that they do. Yes, friends and partners ought to be more accepting of your idiosyncrasies than the general public, but Don’s friends were too quick to shrug and say <i>That’s Don for you</i> while the general public was too quick to say <i>This is a man that needs to be locked up</i>. This dichotomy was no doubt meant to be humorous, but it was just too severe for me to swallow. <br /><br />I have no doubt that readers who enjoyed the first book more than I did will also enjoy the second book more than I did. But I am an asshole, so I could not wait to just be done with this one. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3772742230875233092" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781443435901" href="/book/show/22674895-the-rosie-effect">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7632558-dana?shelf=adult-romance">adult-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7632558-dana?shelf=2014">2014</a>,

              <span id="reviewTextContainer982674667" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13854163413664125357"><br/>As you may be able to tell from my status updates, I was a little frustrated with Rosie in this book. In turn that made me think perhaps this sequel was less enjoyable than the original, but the more I think about it, the more convinced I am that this book is just as good if not better than The Rosie Project. I was just taken for a loop because this book seemed so much more “real” than the first, and real life is hard and awkward and rage inducing.<br/><br/>Its possible that I was being too hard on Rosie,</span>
  <span id="freeText13854163413664125357" style="display:none"><br />As you may be able to tell from my status updates, I was a little frustrated with Rosie in this book. In turn that made me think perhaps this sequel was less enjoyable than the original, but the more I think about it, the more convinced I am that this book is just as good if not better than The Rosie Project. I was just taken for a loop because this book seemed so much more “real” than the first, and real life is hard and awkward and rage inducing.<br /><br />Its possible that I was being too hard on Rosie, I think it is just so much easier to relate to Don, or at least to like Don because he is so transparent. However after closing the book and thinking on it I confirmed my suspicion that Rosie wasn't being a bitch, she was just being herself in a hard situation.<br /><br />While still filled with laugh out loud moments like the original, The Rosie Effect is noticeably more dark, and I have to respect the author for going in this direction. It was a risky move but I think it paid off. I am definitely interested in another installment of the Don and Rosie show.<br /><br /><br /><b>Buy, Borrow or Bin Verdict: Buy</b><br /><br /><br /></span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781922182104" href="/book/show/21844019-the-rosie-effect">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5194069-jenbebookish?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5194069-jenbebookish?shelf=i-expected-more">i-expected-more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1141538436" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17822839548346858033">Ugh.<br/><br/>What a total disappointment. And not just a lil one, but a total train wreck. I can't believe I wasted a day's worth of precious reading time on this. It was just that I kept expecting for it to get better! The first time around was the perfect blend of a slightly irritable, short, straight to the point, and sweet-but-simultaneously-almost-removed way of reporting the story. Don's voice was unusual, but yet still genuine, and despite him being an obviously unusual person, we were still able </span>
  <span id="freeText17822839548346858033" style="display:none">Ugh.<br /><br />What a total disappointment. And not just a lil one, but a total train wreck. I can't believe I wasted a day's worth of precious reading time on this. It was just that I kept expecting for it to get better! The first time around was the perfect blend of a slightly irritable, short, straight to the point, and sweet-but-simultaneously-almost-removed way of reporting the story. Don's voice was unusual, but yet still genuine, and despite him being an obviously unusual person, we were still able to connect with him as readers. This time around it became too much of a good thing. Everything Simsion did the first time around, he tried to do again this time but it was as if this time he just ran out of steam to do it right; he lacked the heart, the sincerity, the humanizing aspects and what was left was this robotic telling of a story from seemingly robotic people. It was just weird, and off. What it sorta felt like to me was that "The Rosie Project" was a novel; something an author put heart and soul into, bringing characters to life and falling in love with them and being invested in their lives and outcomes. One the other hand, "The Rose Effect" felt like it was the quickly jotted down, unedited, unloved and uncared for brother of "The Rosie Project."<br /><br />I would 100% recommend just skipping this one, especially if you loved "The Rosie Project." Just leave The Project fresh in your mind and don't ruin a good thing by warping your perception of Graeme Simsion and his abilities by reading "The Rosie Effect," because thats exactly what it did for me! Truly doesn't even feel like the same person could have written both, it feels more like The Rosie Effect is somebody else's sad attempt at mimicking The Rosie Project.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17822839548346858033" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781922182104" href="/book/show/21844019-the-rosie-effect">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer920930446" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9967416374172020063">I smiled, laughed and got teary eyed in this book just as I did in The Rosie Project because it's fun, funny, sad and just an all-around feel good story . I was thrilled to meet up with Don Tillman and his wife Rosie again. It‘s light hearted in the sense that there are some very funny moments in this book as we see Don trying to cope with married life , and preparing himself to be a father . You just can't imagine the things he does and I certainly don't want to spoil the fun of reading about t</span>
  <span id="freeText9967416374172020063" style="display:none">I smiled, laughed and got teary eyed in this book just as I did in The Rosie Project because it's fun, funny, sad and just an all-around feel good story . I was thrilled to meet up with Don Tillman and his wife Rosie again. It‘s light hearted in the sense that there are some very funny moments in this book as we see Don trying to cope with married life , and preparing himself to be a father . You just can't imagine the things he does and I certainly don't want to spoil the fun of reading about this by telling about them here . Don gets in to considerably more trouble than when he sneaks around trying to steal DNA samples to find out who Rosie's biological father is in the previous book. However, this is more than just a feel good story.<br /><br />He and Rosie seem to be having some communication issues but they are not alone . Don's “normal “ friends ( and those are very big quotation marks ) are having communication issues with their wives as well so it's just not Don. There's a lot of deception going on here but from Don's perspective , he just wants to protect Rosie and things just sort of spin out of control. I would have given it five stars but it just seemed to get a little over the top towards the end . <br /><br /><br />I read this sequel in a little different light than The Rosie Project because I remembered how my GR friend Margi's review touched me where she tells of her personal perspective on the story. Here is her wonderful review <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/726132068?book_show_action=false&amp;page=1">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a> that I hope will make readers think about this book and people with Asperger’s in a different <br />light . Because of Margi’s review, the novel was more than just a light hearted, funny read for me. (The link was included here with Margi's permission.)<br /><br /><br />While Don tries to conform to what people tell him he should be doing or saying, the truth of the matter is that he really can’t and doesn’t change who he is and it is a beautiful thing that Rosie, even though she doubts him at times, loves him for who he is.<br /><br /><br />Thanks to Simon &amp; Schuster and NetGalley for the opportunity to read this advance copy.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14039152828894561288">This was an amusing sequel to <i>The Rosie Project</i>. The socially awkward scientist Don Tillman and his wife, Rosie, are now living in New York and expecting a baby. Don is worried he won't be a good father, so he sets out to get some parenting experience, which leads to a few disasters and damages his relationship with Rosie. Luckily, Don has some friends who can help him resolve the misunderstandings. <br/><br/>This plot hit a lot of the same notes as the first book, including how Don uses his idiosyncrasie</span>
  <span id="freeText14039152828894561288" style="display:none">This was an amusing sequel to <i>The Rosie Project</i>. The socially awkward scientist Don Tillman and his wife, Rosie, are now living in New York and expecting a baby. Don is worried he won't be a good father, so he sets out to get some parenting experience, which leads to a few disasters and damages his relationship with Rosie. Luckily, Don has some friends who can help him resolve the misunderstandings. <br /><br />This plot hit a lot of the same notes as the first book, including how Don uses his idiosyncrasies to solve problems, and that every conflict occurs because Don has trouble interpreting social customs and behaviors, but it's still a sweet, enjoyable novel. Recommended for those who want a lighthearted romantic comedy.<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_965315879" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/965315879" />
    <a title="Ashley - Book Labyrinth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2304814-ashley---book-labyrinth"><img alt="Ashley - Book Labyrinth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1315586541p2/2304814.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/965315879?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley - Book Labyrinth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley - Book Labyrinth" href="/user/show/2304814-ashley---book-labyrinth">Ashley - Book Labyrinth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781443435901" href="/book/show/22674895-the-rosie-effect">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2304814-ashley---book-labyrinth?shelf=my-books">my-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2304814-ashley---book-labyrinth?shelf=adult">adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer965315879" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16262371440879779005">I'm SO UPSET to give this book only two stars. I'm tempted to bump it up to three stars, because there are definitely some good parts to it <i>and</i> because I absolutely loved the first book, but honestly right now it feels like a two star book.<br/><br/>While the first book wasn't perfect, I found it to be utterly charming. Everything about it was so sweet and fun and real. <i>The Rosie Effect</i>, by contrast, feels like ... well, it feels like an author rushing out a sequel to capitalize on the enormous success of</span>
  <span id="freeText16262371440879779005" style="display:none">I'm SO UPSET to give this book only two stars. I'm tempted to bump it up to three stars, because there are definitely some good parts to it <i>and</i> because I absolutely loved the first book, but honestly right now it feels like a two star book.<br /><br />While the first book wasn't perfect, I found it to be utterly charming. Everything about it was so sweet and fun and real. <i>The Rosie Effect</i>, by contrast, feels like ... well, it feels like an author rushing out a sequel to capitalize on the enormous success of the first book. I'm not saying that was the author's intent, but that's what it <i>feels</i> like.<br /><br />Both Rosie and Don clearly have some issues, but it's the way they work together that made the first book work so well. Rosie is a tough character to get, but it seems like she like understands and accepts Don and is making progress in her own life. Don, on the other hand, doesn't logically feel like Rosie is his match, but he connects with her and loves her despite that. Obviously when you have a sequel that's based on a romantic pair you need to throw a wrench in their lives and cause chaos, because otherwise you don't have a story. What I didn't expect was a total reversal of these roles from the first book. I didn't expect the characters to regress.<br /><br />Despite being the titular character, Rosie is basically absent for a lot of this book. She's in the background completing her thesis and generally being every kind of stereotype for an absent-minded shrew of a pregnant woman. Seriously, I wanted to strangle Rosie for the things she was doing and saying. Obviously she's a character with issues, but she was also sweet and fun and accepting. I didn't see any of that here, and it really upset me to see the author write Rosie this way.<br /><br />There are so many other things that made me dislike this one. Don's actions were beyond ridiculous. There are the social faux pas that I would expect from his character, and then there were things that went WAY over the top. There's also the way Gene was part of this book, of which I would say there was way too much of his character -- there was really no point to his part in the story. And then, probably most importantly, is the fact that this book doesn't really have much of a plot. It's all about marital problems, lack of communication, and a crazed social worker (surprise! it's a female character acting completely unprofessionally and illogically) taking out her own issues on Don. Of course things happen, but it really feels like one long ramble with very little purpose to it.<br /><br />I was so looking forward to this one after enjoying <i>The Rosie Project</i> so much, but honestly I would suggest stopping after the first book. This was such a disappointment.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16262371440879779005" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText8685944171421077524" style="display:none">I loved the second installment of this series!     <a title="Jennifer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2473504-jennifer"><img alt="Jennifer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1394406877p2/2473504.jpg" /></a>

        <a title="Jennifer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer" href="/user/show/2473504-jennifer">Jennifer</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

          </div>
