        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer926480333" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4616130053870455375"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21844019.The_Rosie_Effect__Don_Tillman__2_' title='The Rosie Effect (Don Tillman #2) by Graeme Simsion' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Rosie Effect</a> is the second installment in the Don Tillman series written by author <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1895943.Graeme_Simsion' title='Graeme Simsion' rel='nofollow noopener'>Graeme Simsion</a>.<br/> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1418209288ra/12706284.gif' width='400' height='270' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I <b>adored</b> the first book <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16181775.The_Rosie_Project__Don_Tillman__1_' title='The Rosie Project (Don Tillman #1) by Graeme Simsion' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Rosie Project</a>, so imagine my disappointment when <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21844019.The_Rosie_Effect__Don_Tillman__2_' title='The Rosie Effect (Don Tillman #2) by Graeme Simsion' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Rosie Effect</a> failed to live up to it's predecessor. That is my opinion at least. Please note though that three stars isn't horrible! It was still a good read, but when compared to the endearing, sweet, and funny story that came before it, there's just no comparison. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21844019.The_Rosie_Effect__Don_Tillman__2_' title='The Rosie Effect (Don Tillman #2) by Graeme Simsion' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Rosie Effect</a> was a bit more serious, as the t</span>
  <span id="freeText4616130053870455375" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21844019.The_Rosie_Effect__Don_Tillman__2_" title="The Rosie Effect (Don Tillman #2) by Graeme Simsion" rel="nofollow noopener">The Rosie Effect</a> is the second installment in the Don Tillman series written by author <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1895943.Graeme_Simsion" title="Graeme Simsion" rel="nofollow noopener">Graeme Simsion</a>.<br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1418209288ra/12706284.gif" width="400" height="270" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I <b>adored</b> the first book <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16181775.The_Rosie_Project__Don_Tillman__1_" title="The Rosie Project (Don Tillman #1) by Graeme Simsion" rel="nofollow noopener">The Rosie Project</a>, so imagine my disappointment when <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21844019.The_Rosie_Effect__Don_Tillman__2_" title="The Rosie Effect (Don Tillman #2) by Graeme Simsion" rel="nofollow noopener">The Rosie Effect</a> failed to live up to it's predecessor. That is my opinion at least. Please note though that three stars isn't horrible! It was still a good read, but when compared to the endearing, sweet, and funny story that came before it, there's just no comparison. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21844019.The_Rosie_Effect__Don_Tillman__2_" title="The Rosie Effect (Don Tillman #2) by Graeme Simsion" rel="nofollow noopener">The Rosie Effect</a> was a bit more serious, as the theme of falling in love has now transitioned into making a marriage work and preparing for the logistics of a traditional family. So naturally, it's not going to be all butterflies and rainbows this time around. But even so, the writing felt much dryer. I didn't laugh much at all, or smile really. I just felt sad for most of the characters much of the time, even when the crises Don got himself into were likely intended to add humor. However, the ending had the same urgency and fast pace as the first book did, with our hero Don finally concluding the perfect way to connect with his love Rosie, which I appreciated. It just wasn't enough for me to bump up my personal rating. <br><br>If you're a fan of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16181775.The_Rosie_Project__Don_Tillman__1_" title="The Rosie Project (Don Tillman #1) by Graeme Simsion" rel="nofollow noopener">The Rosie Project</a> and have been looking forward to this one, please don't let this review stop you! Sometimes, one's expectations get in the way of overall enjoyment, and I'm realistic enough to accept that this may have been my situation. If you do check it out, let me know what you think! Happy Reading!!!<br><br><b>My favorite quote:</b><br><i>“Watch some kids, watch them play. You’ll see they’re just little adults, only they don’t know all the rules and tricks yet.”</i><br><br>The Don Tillman series includes the following installments as of January 2015:<br>#1-<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16181775.The_Rosie_Project__Don_Tillman__1_" title="The Rosie Project (Don Tillman #1) by Graeme Simsion" rel="nofollow noopener">The Rosie Project</a><br>#2-<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21844019.The_Rosie_Effect__Don_Tillman__2_" title="The Rosie Effect (Don Tillman #2) by Graeme Simsion" rel="nofollow noopener">The Rosie Effect</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16181775.The_Rosie_Project__Don_Tillman__1_" title="The Rosie Project (Don Tillman #1) by Graeme Simsion" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1371651741s/16181775.jpg" alt="The Rosie Project (Don Tillman #1) by Graeme Simsion" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21844019.The_Rosie_Effect__Don_Tillman__2_" title="The Rosie Effect (Don Tillman #2) by Graeme Simsion" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1396602020s/21844019.jpg" alt="The Rosie Effect (Don Tillman #2) by Graeme Simsion" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

<div id="review_900550008" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/900550008" />
    <a title="Marianne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5067228-marianne"><img alt="Marianne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1303027210p2/5067228.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/900550008?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marianne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marianne" href="/user/show/5067228-marianne">Marianne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781922182104" href="/book/show/21844019-the-rosie-effect">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer900550008" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4461831888907918605">The Rosie Effect is the second novel by Australian author and playwright, Graeme Simsion, and the sequel to his highly popular novel, The Rosie Project. Now married, Don and Rosie are living in a cramped New York apartment while, as a visiting professor at Columbia, Don continues his research on alcoholic mice and Rosie studies to gain her MD qualification. Don’s friend, Gene, a geneticist and serial adulterer, has finally exhausted his wife’s tolerance for philandering and been thrown out, so D</span>
  <span id="freeText4461831888907918605" style="display:none">The Rosie Effect is the second novel by Australian author and playwright, Graeme Simsion, and the sequel to his highly popular novel, The Rosie Project. Now married, Don and Rosie are living in a cramped New York apartment while, as a visiting professor at Columbia, Don continues his research on alcoholic mice and Rosie studies to gain her MD qualification. Don’s friend, Gene, a geneticist and serial adulterer, has finally exhausted his wife’s tolerance for philandering and been thrown out, so Don invites him to stay with them, unwisely neglecting to check with Rosie first. And before he gets a chance to do so, Rosie announces that they are having a baby.<br /> <br />Don’s solution to multiple problems (accommodation deficit with respect to the imminent arrival of an overseas guest and an eventual addition to the family; a laundry confrontation with a neighbour; a twice-daily beer-related commitment; financial stress due to the (Don-induced) loss of employment at a cocktail bar; the need to keep Rosie’s stress levels at a minimum) is a wonderfully elegant example of lateral thinking that only someone of his extraordinary talents could manage.<br />Gene’s advice on fatherhood is mostly sound, but unfortunately rather too vague for Don, who manages to get himself into trouble involving police, counsellors and support groups. <br /><br />Mindful of the results of Rosie’s own research into the effects of stress during pregnancy, Don wants to spare her any anxiety and eventually tangles himself (and several others) in a web of deceit. His eccentric manner of dealing with Rosie’s pregnancy and his own impending fatherhood ends up threatening their happiness together. Luckily, he has friends (six, now!) who care and his boy’s night out group (recently expanded to include a rock star, and a psychology professor in addition to a refrigeration engineer) provide unique support.<br /><br />In Don, Simsion has created a character who is easy to love: he cares about his friends, is completely guileless, somewhat innocent and totally without malice. He has wholehearted enthusiasm for, and dedication to, any project he decides to take on. Simsion introduces a few new characters and expands on characters that readers will remember from The Rosie Project, so there are a few sub-plots keeping Don busy. This novel is filled with an abundance of hilarious situations that will have the reader snickering, groaning and laughing out loud as Don navigates his way through dinners (the Bluefin Tuna Incident), toddler observation (the Playground Incident), counselling sessions (the Good Fathers Project), research projects (the Lesbian Mothers Project), errors in judgement (the Second Ultrasound Misunderstanding), encounters with Loud Woman, Bubonic Plague Woman and an opinionated social worker, and tries to reinstate the Standardised Meal System (pregnancy version). <br /><br />Don’s instinctive solution to any problem is a spreadsheet, and his Baby Project bathroom-tile spreadsheet sounds fascinating. Ditto Jim’s soundproof crib. There are Gregory Peck impersonations, Rosie impersonations, men sharing their deepest secrets, a perfect anniversary celebration engineered for Don by Rosie, and, of course, bouts of morning sickness which elicit Don’s logical (if unsympathetic-sounding) response: “Feeling unwell is normal in pregnancy. It’s almost certainly a good sign.…..Your body is probably assembling some critical component, such as an arm, and is minimising the possibility of toxins disrupting the process.” <br /><br />Simsion’s latest novel takes a light-hearted look at medical research projects, sustainable meal choices, social workers, pregnancy and of course, fatherhood. Apart from the many laughs, there are also a few lump-in-the-throat moments and readers who loved The Rosie Project will not be disappointed. A funny, moving and sometimes thought-provoking read. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4461831888907918605" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer8848553043277325774">I must admit I was a bit disappointed in this book which is - in my opinion - nothing like The Rosie Project. It was fascinating being back inside Don's head, but I couldn't really stand how the author was consistenly trying to create funny situations that turned out not being that funny at all. I didn't feel a connection to the story nor Don or Rosie throughout most of the book, mostly because I didn't agree with their decisions which I considered silly and inconsiderate. <br/>I am a bit flabbergast</span>
  <span id="freeText8848553043277325774" style="display:none">I must admit I was a bit disappointed in this book which is - in my opinion - nothing like The Rosie Project. It was fascinating being back inside Don's head, but I couldn't really stand how the author was consistenly trying to create funny situations that turned out not being that funny at all. I didn't feel a connection to the story nor Don or Rosie throughout most of the book, mostly because I didn't agree with their decisions which I considered silly and inconsiderate. <br />I am a bit flabbergasted at how much this book actually disappointed me. There were several chapters where my mind started to drift because I didn't really care for the story, which is completely opposite to my reaction to The Rosie Project (which I adored!). This book didn't have any of the sass and endearing scenes that we get in the first book; in contrast, it was boring and predictable and contained too many foolish scenarios that I didn't really buy into. <br />In my opinion, this sequel should not have been written because it didn't add anything new and refreshing to the story - which is sad.</span>

  <span id="freeText4115448132475491639" style="display:none">In the Rosie Project, I fell in love with Don and Rosie, this author, and the narrator of the audiobook. Now again as Don and Rosie are living in NYC and expecting a baby, all the same elements are there. Don is on top of making sure Rosie stays healthy and knows what's best for the baby--what he doesn't know he reads up on-- but can't seem to feel anything emotionally for the fetus yet because ya can't get that from a book. <div id="review_900618238" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/900618238" />
    <a title="Kathryn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2825213-kathryn"><img alt="Kathryn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483412885p2/2825213.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/900618238?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathryn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathryn" href="/user/show/2825213-kathryn">Kathryn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781922182104" href="/book/show/21844019-the-rosie-effect">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2825213-kathryn?shelf=australian-authors">australian-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2825213-kathryn?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2825213-kathryn?shelf=released-2014">released-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2825213-kathryn?shelf=reading-list-2014">reading-list-2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer900618238" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12179438498859160602">In The Rosie Effect we meet some of the same characters as in The Rosie Project - Don is just the same - at times sweet, at times infuriating, always logical while Rosie is somewhat pre-occupied with her thesis, her pregnancy and Don’s interference in how she lives because of her pregnancy. Although they are now living in New York, Don’s good friend from Melbourne, Gene, comes to stay for a period. He is NOT the same Gene we knew previously - he is full of (mostly) sound advice for Don. How Don </span>
  <span id="freeText12179438498859160602" style="display:none">In The Rosie Effect we meet some of the same characters as in The Rosie Project - Don is just the same - at times sweet, at times infuriating, always logical while Rosie is somewhat pre-occupied with her thesis, her pregnancy and Don’s interference in how she lives because of her pregnancy. Although they are now living in New York, Don’s good friend from Melbourne, Gene, comes to stay for a period. He is NOT the same Gene we knew previously - he is full of (mostly) sound advice for Don. How Don interprets this advice is where some of his problems arise.<br /><br />I didn’t enjoy this as much as The Rosie Project and am not sure whether this is due to the sequel often not being as good as the first - I guess if the first of something is new and exciting, the second is never going to be new or as exciting.<br /><br />I also felt that the whole thing degenerated into some kind of farce about 4/5 of the way through. The whole book is filled with unlikely situations, but events around this time just seemed to be one step too far for me and pushed me over the edge of disbelief. And around the 2/3 mark there was also a situation which I just didn't feel was plausible - so that may have been when I started to disengage a little.<br /><br />I was very engaged with the book early on, and chuckled my way through and was thinking it would be worth at least 4 stars, but parts of the last third spoiled it a little for me, although the ending was satisfying, so I decided on 3.5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12179438498859160602" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a title="Jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica" href="/user/show/202724-jessica">Jessica</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781476767314" href="/book/show/22546489-the-rosie-effect">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/202724-jessica?shelf=literaryfiction">literaryfiction</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1126945267" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12529334879743872141">Hm. This book was very stressful for me. While the first one was very madcap and very much a rom-com (and had originally been written as a screenplay) this one took a darker turn that I was not expecting. <br/><br/>There were plenty of misunderstandings due to Don taking everything literally and some of them funny, but some of them either mean or a bit scary. The police and mental health professionals are involved, not to spoil anything but just to give you an idea. Rosie is less likable because after a y</span>
  <span id="freeText12529334879743872141" style="display:none">Hm. This book was very stressful for me. While the first one was very madcap and very much a rom-com (and had originally been written as a screenplay) this one took a darker turn that I was not expecting. <br /><br />There were plenty of misunderstandings due to Don taking everything literally and some of them funny, but some of them either mean or a bit scary. The police and mental health professionals are involved, not to spoil anything but just to give you an idea. Rosie is less likable because after a year of marriage seems to have LESS understanding for Don and less appreciation for his gifts, and I've never liked his "friend" Gene. I do adore Dave and Sonia, and Don's new friend George, a semi-retired rock star, is one of the best bits of the book. I spent the last third of the book in a state of great anxiety, worrying that things would not turn out all right, and then felt that the ending was over far too quick. I will say that I wasn't disappointed in the ending, and there were a couple of nice twists that I was not expecting. For a while I worried that Simsion was trying to make the point that, Sure we all loved Don in THE ROSIE PROJECT, but actually being married to him would be a nightmare and would never work out, which would be a pretty shitty thing to do. Simsion is not that mean, though, so you can rest easy! <br /><br />Overall I enjoyed the book and I'm glad he wrote it and I read it. It just . . . wasn't quite what I was expecting and didn't delight me quite as much the first one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12529334879743872141" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17229514173413043960">The rare equals-the-original sequel. Don Tillman is the perennial nerd-in-love. A hopeless but not romantic fella who wins his gal, and offspring, pretty much from the getgo. Rosie, forgive her state, is a pill, and so Don is forgiven for becoming a man in the sense of, well, what is a dude's role? He, and we, find out, and I hope that this soon becomes a series of films or something: the Australian Sheldon Cooper longs to be cast! What could be baby-talk actually morphs into a story of Fathers </span>
  <span id="freeText17229514173413043960" style="display:none">The rare equals-the-original sequel. Don Tillman is the perennial nerd-in-love. A hopeless but not romantic fella who wins his gal, and offspring, pretty much from the getgo. Rosie, forgive her state, is a pill, and so Don is forgiven for becoming a man in the sense of, well, what is a dude's role? He, and we, find out, and I hope that this soon becomes a series of films or something: the Australian Sheldon Cooper longs to be cast! What could be baby-talk actually morphs into a story of Fathers and Sons, as the tight group of male pals transcend slapstick to be genuinely affecting by their own right. A very strange and surprising turn, this is. Hats off, Mr. Simsion!<br /><br />Bottom line: so its a tad bubbly, a little bit flighty, but as enchanting as "Project"--heck, even more so!</span>

<div id="review_1066667572" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1066667572" />
    <a title="Carolyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19559507-carolyn"><img alt="Carolyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546411572p2/19559507.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1066667572?book_show_action=true">Sep 28, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carolyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carolyn" href="/user/show/19559507-carolyn">Carolyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/22447256-the-rosie-effect">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19559507-carolyn?shelf=australian-author">australian-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19559507-carolyn?shelf=humour">humour</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19559507-carolyn?shelf=relationships">relationships</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1066667572" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14926638265780955028">Rosie and Don and now happily married, living in New York where Don is a visiting Assistant Professor at Columbia and Rosie is trying to finish writing her PhD thesis while also starting her medical studies. On top of that they still have their part time job making cocktails in a down town bar. Don is learning to embrace spontaneity and life is hectic but fun until Rosie drops a bombshell that sends Don into a spin. <br/><br/>It's no secret to those who haven't yet read this book that Don and Rosie are ex</span>
  <span id="freeText14926638265780955028" style="display:none">Rosie and Don and now happily married, living in New York where Don is a visiting Assistant Professor at Columbia and Rosie is trying to finish writing her PhD thesis while also starting her medical studies. On top of that they still have their part time job making cocktails in a down town bar. Don is learning to embrace spontaneity and life is hectic but fun until Rosie drops a bombshell that sends Don into a spin. <br /><br />It's no secret to those who haven't yet read this book that Don and Rosie are expecting a baby. How Don copes with the news and tries to prepare himself to welcome this addition to his family results in some hilarious scenarios - if reading this in public be warned that you may experience some seriously L-O-L moments. Trying to prepare for the baby and to avoid causing Rosie any stress result in some very funny moments where Don's lack of sensitivity to social cues and his logical approach gets him into some messy situations. Both Don's old and new friends try to give him advice, but only make matters worse and it is they who end up benefiting from Don's logical view of the world in sorting out their own relationship problems.<br /><br />My only small gripe with the book is that Rosie's voice is not heard as clearly in this book as in the previous one. When Don first meets Rosie she is witty and quirky, but in this book she seems more subdued and less in tune with Don's feelings. Knowing how Don likes to plan everything down to the nth degree, I was surprised that she would spring the announcement of an unexpected pregnancy on him without carefully preparing him for the news first. Also knowing his difficulty with social interactions and lack of contact with children, she might have predicted that he would have trouble connecting with an unborn child and helped more to pave the way. To some extent Rosie seems to have lost that understanding and empathy with Don that she had in the previous book and Don is left floundering around trying to work it all out on his own. However that aside, it was an excellent sequel to the Rosie Project and I look forward with anticipation to the next episode in the lives of Don and co. 4.5★</span>
  <a data-text-id="14926638265780955028" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2524893468" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1184774000676813972">Ha ha ha. <br/><br/>Although I had read “The Rosie Project” a couple of years ago, I typically do not often read sequels. In this case, I can say that I was wrong and should have read this book sooner.<br/><br/>As soon as I started to read, I remember how much I enjoyed the Don Tillman character. Yes his lack of social ability and his over exuberance on technical material, reveals the positive-negative traits of a person with Aspergers. He annoys and he charms. However, all this quirkiness, coupled with a lot of ac</span>
  <span id="freeText1184774000676813972" style="display:none">Ha ha ha. <br /><br />Although I had read “The Rosie Project” a couple of years ago, I typically do not often read sequels. In this case, I can say that I was wrong and should have read this book sooner.<br /><br />As soon as I started to read, I remember how much I enjoyed the Don Tillman character. Yes his lack of social ability and his over exuberance on technical material, reveals the positive-negative traits of a person with Aspergers. He annoys and he charms. However, all this quirkiness, coupled with a lot of accidental humour made this book a fun read.<br /><br />Rosie is expecting their first child while trying to finish her degree at Columbia University in New York. She is totally stressed. Don, unsure of becoming a father is tested and tests himself through the similar mayhem found in the first book. It’s not a copy of the first and at times, far fetched and sometimes very believable. The cast of characters including the rock star George who lives above, the bungling Dave and the womanizing Gene make for a lot of fun reading.<br /><br />Totally fun entertainment. </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1080082799" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11525988003184406959"><b>1.5 stars - I didn't like it.</b><br/><br/>This seriously disappointing sequel to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17281240.The_Rosie_Project' title='The Rosie Project by Graeme Simsion' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Rosie Project</a>, should have actually been titled <i>The Baby Project</i>. This more appropriate suggestion is not a spoiler, as we find out about the baby 7 minutes into the book, and that is all we hear about for the next 100 pages. Baby this, baby that, baby baby baby. What is beyond the first 110ish pages, I cannot say, because that is where I DNF'd this baby.<br/>-------------------------------------------<br/><b>Favorite Quote:</b> N/A.<br/><br/><b>First Se</b></span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('LHZlk/UddoGbcM0Nn8YQaFo3YJpkxyZizA5YWV3Jnmi8tFg3oGGK5hnDyz3Lw7lRg1m3y2j/+nmn1JFIgDIAnQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Lt2bOvNG20q4NJYg1WUQSqi4pgh3Pjdln4mBy4X0Y7S+H6aepjonLTqHkBCBYLlzcdZxWXsG6370U0jaWA/9QQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer8355521602845713694">Graeme Simsion is a former IT consultant and the author of two nonfiction books on database design who decided, at the age of fifty, to turn his hand to fiction. His first novel, <i>The Rosie Project,</i> was published in 2013 and translation rights have been sold in forty languages. Movie rights have been optioned to Sony Pictures. The sequel, <i>The Rosie Effect</i>, is also a bestseller, with total sales of </span>
  <span id="freeText8355521602845713694" style="display:none">Graeme Simsion is a former IT consultant and the author of two nonfiction books on database design who decided, at the age of fifty, to turn his hand to fiction. His first novel, <i>The Rosie Project,</i> was published in 2013 and translation rights have been sold in forty languages. Movie rights have been optioned to Sony Pictures. The sequel, <i>The Rosie Effect</i>, is also a bestseller, with total sales of the two novels approaching five million. <br />Graeme's third novel was <i>The Best of Adam Sharp</i>, a story of a love affair re-kindled - and its consequences. Movie rights have been optioned by Vocab Films with Toni Collette attached to play the role of Adam's great lost love, Angelina.<br />Graeme's fourth novel, <i>Two Steps Forward</i> is a story of renewal set on the Camino de Santiago, written with his wife, Anne Buist, whose own books include <i>Medea's Curse, Dangerous to Know</i> and <i>This I would Kill for</i>. Movie rights have been optioned by Fox Searchlight with Ellen DeGeneris to produce.</span>
